late to the party, but for those that are afraid of burning chicken/crust while frying....an old trick is to shallow fry them(oil only covers half the chicken; turn when one side is golden brown and repeat for the other side) on high heat, then turn the heat down to medium/medium-low so they simmer in the oil. you are assured that the chicken is done while also preventing a burned crust.

I know it may not be appropriate, but I've always found that adding eggs to a flour based batter tends to make the food too "grease-absorbing". I prefer to stick to only egg whites if you really need the eggy texture, and use the yolks separated instead as a part of the marinade/rub if you really need the yolk flavor. Otherwise, I usually just take out the eggs and use water or milk instead.

I have a recipe for those "potato mushrooms" left behind by the Kitchen Aid apple peeler attachment. I received it as a gift. I left it in the box for four years in a closet. I would never need a machine to peel fruit or vegetables. I never cook for more than 8... But, I did once need to peel about 20 pounds of potatoes, so I pulled out the device last Christmas and went for it. I was surprised to learn it even had a spiralizing feature. Those mushroom potato butter were a cute and funny surprise to find. So, of course, I played with them. In the end, they make a really fine roast potato in the shape of fungi for two servings. Every 20 lbs of potatoes... two slight servings. Cute as a button!

Alas, learned the hard way that if you're going to marinate the chicken in a traditional brine, it will _fully_ soak up however much salt you put in there, so only use a little bit. Good thing I did a small batch to test the recipe first.  Weirdly enough, I forgot the egg the first time and it turned out super-crispy. The next time I made this, I added the egg and it became much softer. Either way, this batter does a phenomenal job of keeping in the moisture. I used boneless chicken breast to do nuggets and they were still juicy the next day, when white meat isn't usually juicy even 20 minutes after cooking.

As someone who deep-fries far too much at home, I've found that a large steel pot and a spider skimmer with a bamboo handle is a good way to do it if you're worried. The one I use is an old Farberware stockpot. Still only 2 inches of oil, but it only overflows if you're doing something *very* wrong. Also, most of the splatter gets on the pot.

Hey Babish, saw you wearing gloves while frying. Just a heads up: Gloves are actually worse to wear while frying. You can get oil off your skin faster and easier than you can get it off a glove, and it will stick to the glove longer and just burn through and burn you longer. When I was in Culinary Arts, they would scold anyone who used gloves while frying. It just makes it more dangerous.

My folk had guests over so they just told me there was sausage in the freezer and I just had to cook it. I changed into my satin, incredibly comfortable PJs that I never wore closed up and began heating up the pan with oil in it to then, yes, drop the frozen sausage in the hot oil. Obviously it crackled and exploded, spraying me all over my bare chest and stomach but honestlly I was so tired (whole night of staying awake in the train cart because honestly fuck those beds) and I knew before hand that it would happen that it literally registered like rain drops and nothing more. So imagine a large dude, dopely staring at a sausage in a pan as oil splashes on him but doesn't seem to register. I fried some eggs to go with the sausage, ate up and went to sleep.

I am going to go against Babish here and recommend absolutely NO ONE deep fry anything in a skillet or frying pan on an open flame stove top, no matter how big.  You're just asking for a disaster with that.  If you have to deep fry at home (and Babish is right, it should scare the shit out of you, as many people end up in hospitals because of it) use a dedicated deep fryer unit, or a large pot with at least two inches of clearance between the oil and the lip.  I understand Babish maybe  thought he had to use that frying pan for the camera angle, but that was simply irresponsible and sets a bad example.
